Every\\n192: \\t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\\n193: \\t// processing set.\\n194: \\tqueue Queue[t]\\n195: \\n196: \\t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\\n197: \\tdirty sets.Set[t]\\n198: \\n199: \\t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\\n200: \\t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\\n201: \\t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\\n202: \\t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\\n203: \\tprocessing sets.Set[t]\\n204: \\n205: \\tcond *sync.Cond\\n206: \\n207: \\tshuttingDown bool\\n208: \\tdrain        bool\\n209: \\n210: \\tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\\n211: \\n212: \\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\\n213: \\tclock                      clock.WithTicker\\n214: \\n215: \\t// wg manages goroutines started by the queue to allow graceful shutdown\\n216: \\t// ShutDown() will wait for goroutines to exit before returning.\\n217: \\twg sync.WaitGroup\\n218: \\n219: \\tstopCh chan struct{}\\n220: \\t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\\n221: \\tstopOnce sync.Once\\n222: }\\n223: \\n224: // Add marks item as needing processing. When the queue is shutdown new\\n225: // items will silently be ignored and not queued or marked as dirty for\\n226: // reprocessing.\\n227: func (q *Typed[T]) Add(item T) {\\n228: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n229: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n230: \\tif q.shuttingDown {\\n231: \\t\\treturn\\n232: \\t}\\n233: \\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\\n234: \\t\\t// the same item is added again before it is processed, call the Touch\\n235: \\t\\t// function if the queue cares about it (for e.g, reset its priority)\\n236: \\t\\tif !q.processing.Has(item) {\\n237: \\t\\t\\tq.queue.Touch(item)\\n238: \\t\\t}\\n239: \\t\\treturn\\n240: \\t}\\n241: \\n242: \\tq.metrics.add(item)\\n243: \\n244: \\tq.dirty.Insert(item)\\n245: \\tif q.processing.Has(item) {\\n246: \\t\\treturn\\n247: \\t}\\n248: \\n249: \\tq.queue.Push(item)\\n250: \\tq.cond.Signal()\\n251: }\\n252: \\n253: // Len returns the current queue length, for informational purposes only. You\\n254: // shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\\n255: // value, that can't be synchronized properly.\\n256: func (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\\n257: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n258: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n259: \\treturn q.queue.Len()\\n260: }\\n261: \\n262: // Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\\n263: // the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\\n264: // have finished processing it.\\n265: func (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\\n266: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n267: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n268: \\tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\\n269: \\t\\tq.cond.Wait()\\n270: \\t}\\n271: \\tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\\n272: \\t\\t// We must be shutting down.\\n273: \\t\\treturn *new(T), true\\n274: \\t}\\n275: \\n276: \\titem = q.queue.Pop()\\n277: \\n278: \\tq.metrics.get(item)\\n279: \\n280: \\tq.processing.Insert(item)\\n281: \\tq.dirty.Delete(item)\\n282: \\n283: \\treturn item, false\\n284: }\\n285: \\n286: // Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\\n287: // while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\\n288: // re-processing.\\n289: func (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\\n290: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n291: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n292: \\n293: \\tq.metrics.done(item)\\n294: \\n295: \\tq.processing.Delete(item)\\n296: \\tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\\n297: \\t\\tq.queue.Push(item)\\n298: \\t\\tq.cond.Signal()\\n299: \\t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\\n300: \\t\\tq.cond.Signal()\\n301: \\t}\\n302: }\\n303: \\n304: // ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\\n305: // goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\\n306: // empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\\n307: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\\n308: \\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\\n309: \\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\\n310: \\t\\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\\n311: \\t})\\n312: \\n313: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n314: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n315: \\n316: \\tq.drain = false\\n317: \\tq.shuttingDown = true\\n318: \\tq.cond.Broadcast()\\n319: }\\n320: \\n321: // ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\\n322: // in the queue have been processed.\\n323: // ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\\n324: // ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\\n325: // Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, otherwise\\n326: // ShutDownWithDrain will block indefinitely.\\n327: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\\n328: \\tdefer q.wg.Wait()\\n329: \\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\\n330: \\t\\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\\n331: \\t})\\n332: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n333: \\tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\\n334: \\n335: \\tq.drain = true\\n336: \\tq.shuttingDown = true\\n337: \\tq.cond.Broadcast()\\n338: \\n339: \\tfor q.processing.Len() != 0 && q.drain {\\n340: \\t\\tq.cond.Wait()\\n341: \\t}\\n342: }\\n343: \\n344: func (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\\n345: \\tq.cond.L.Lock()\\n346: \\tdefer constructs a new named workqueue\n140: // with the ability to customize different properties for testing purposes\n141: func newQueueWithConfig[T comparable](config TypedQueueConfig[T], updatePeriod time.Duration) *Typed[T] {\n142: \tmetricsProvider := globalMetricsProvider\n143: \tif config.MetricsProvider != nil {\n144: \t\tmetricsProvider = config.MetricsProvider\n145: \t}\n146: \n147: \tif config.Clock == nil {\n148: \t\tconfig.Clock = clock.RealClock{}\n149: \t}\n150: \n151: \tif config.Queue == nil {\n152: \t\tconfig.Queue = DefaultQueue[T]()\n153: \t}\n154: \n155: \treturn newQueue[T comparable](c clock.WithTicker, queue Queue[T], metrics queueMetrics[T], updatePeriod time.Duration) *Typed[T] {\n164: \tt := &Typed[T]{\n165: \t\tclock:                      c,\n166: \t\tqueue:                      queue,\n167: \t\tdirty:                      sets.Set[T]{},\n168: \t\tprocessing:                 sets.Set[T]{},\n169: \t\tcond:                       sync.NewCond(&sync.Mutex{}),\n170: \t\tmetrics:                    metrics,\n171: \t\tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod: updatePeriod,\n172: \t\tstopCh:                     make(chan struct{}),\n173: \t}\n174: \n175: \t// Don't start the goroutine for a type of noMetrics so we don't consume\n176: \t// resources unnecessarily\n177: \tif _, ok := metrics.(noMetrics[T]); !ok {\n178: \t\tt.wg.Go(t.updateUnfinishedWorkLoop)\n179: \t}\n180: \n181: \treturn t\n182: }\n183: \n184: const defaultUnfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod = 500 * time.Millisecond\n185: \n186: // Type is a work queue (see the package comment).\n187: // Deprecated: Use Typed instead.\n188: type Type = Typed[any]\n189: \n190: type Typed[t comparable] struct {\n191: \t// queue defines the order in which we will work on items. Every\n192: \t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\n193: \t// processing set.\n194: \tqueue Queue[t]\n195: \n196: \t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\n197: \tdirty sets.Set[t]\n198: \n199: \t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\n200: \t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. When we finish\n201: \t// processing something and remove it from this set, we'll check if\n202: \t// it's in the dirty set, and if so, add it to the queue.\n203: \tprocessing sets.Set[t]\n204: \n205: \tcond *sync.Cond\n206: \n207: \tshuttingDown bool\n208: \tdrain        bool\n209: \n210: \tmetrics queueMetrics[t]\n211: \n212: \tunfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod time.Duration\n213: \tclock                      clock.WithTicker\n214: \n215: \t// wg manages goroutines started by the queue to allow graceful shutdown\n216: \t// ShutDown() will wait for goroutines to exit before returning.\n217: \twg sync.WaitGroup\n218: \n219: \tstopCh chan struct{}\n220: \t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\n221: \tstopOnce sync.Once\n222: }\n223: \n224: // Add marks item as needing processing. When the queue is shutdown new\n225: // items will silently be ignored and not queued or marked as dirty for\n226: // reprocessing.\n227: func (q *Typed[T]) Add(item T) {\n228: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n229: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n230: \tif q.shuttingDown {\n231: \t\treturn\n232: \t}\n233: \tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n234: \t\t// the same item is added again before it is processed, call the Touch\n235: \t\t// function if the queue cares about it (for e.g, reset its priority)\n236: \t\tif !q.processing.Has(item) {\n237: \t\t\tq.queue.Touch(item)\n238: \t\t}\n239: \t\treturn\n240: \t}\n241: \n242: \tq.metrics.add(item)\n243: \n244: \tq.dirty.Insert(item)\n245: \tif q.processing.Has(item) {\n246: \t\treturn\n247: \t}\n248: \n249: \tq.queue.Push(item)\n250: \tq.cond.Signal()\n251: }\n252: \n253: // Len returns the current queue length, for informational purposes only. You\n254: // shouldn't e.g. gate a call to Add() or Get() on Len() being a particular\n255: // value, that can't be synchronized properly.\n256: func (q *Typed[T]) Len() int {\n257: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n258: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n259: \treturn q.queue.Len()\n260: }\n261: \n262: // Get blocks until it can return an item to be processed. If shutdown = true,\n263: // the caller should end their goroutine. You must call Done with item when you\n264: // have finished processing it.\n265: func (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n266: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n267: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n268: \tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n269: \t\tq.cond.Wait()\n270: \t}\n271: \tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n272: \t\t// We must be shutting down.\n273: \t\treturn *new(T), true\n274: \t}\n275: \n276: \titem = q.queue.Pop()\n277: \n278: \tq.metrics.get(item)\n279: \n280: \tq.processing.Insert(item)\n281: \tq.dirty.Delete(item)\n282: \n283: \treturn item, false\n284: }\n285: \n286: // Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n287: // while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n288: // re-processing.\n289: func (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n290: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n291: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n292: \n293: \tq.metrics.done(item)\n294: \n295: \tq.processing.Delete(item)\n296: \tif q.dirty.Has(item) {\n297: \t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n298: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n299: \t} else if q.processing.Len() == 0 {\n300: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n301: \t}\n302: }\n303: \n304: // ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. Worker\n305: // goroutines will continue processing items in the queue until it is\n306: // empty and then receive the shutdown signal.\n307: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n308: \tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n309: \tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n310: \t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n311: \t})\n312: \n313: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n314: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n315: \n316: \tq.drain = false\n317: \tq.shuttingDown = true\n318: \tq.cond.Broadcast()\n319: }\n320: \n321: // ShutDownWithDrain is equivalent to ShutDown but waits until all items\n322: // in the queue have been processed.\n323: // ShutDown can be called after ShutDownWithDrain to force\n324: // ShutDownWithDrain to stop waiting.\n325: // Workers must call Done on an item after processing it, otherwise\n326: // ShutDownWithDrain will block indefinitely.\n327: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDownWithDrain() {\n328: \tdefer q.wg.Wait()\n329: \tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n330: \t\tdefer close(q.stopCh)\n331: \t})\n332: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n333: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n334: \n335: \tq.drain = true\n336: \tq.shuttingDown = true\n337: \tq.cond.Broadcast()\n338: \n339: \tfor q.processing.Len() != 0 && q.drain {\n340: \t\tq.cond.Wait()\n341: \t}\n342: }\n343: \n344: func (q *Typed[T]) ShuttingDown() bool {\n345: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n346: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n347: \n348: \treturn q.shuttingDown\n349: }\n350: \n351: func (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWork() {\n352: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n353: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n354: \tif !q.shuttingDown {\n355: \t\tq.metrics.updateUnfinishedWork()\n356: \t}\n357: }\n358: \n359: func (q *Typed[T]) updateUnfinishedWorkLoop() {\n360: \tt := q.clock.NewTicker(q.unfinishedWorkUpdatePeriod)\n361: \tdefer t.Stop()\n362: \tfor {\n363: \t\tselect {\n364: \t\tcase across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. The system is organized in a layered architecture:\\n\\n**Core Queue Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go):**\\nThe foundation is the TypedInterface which defines the basic work queue operations: Add(item), Get() returning (item, shutdown), Done(item), Len(), ShutDown(), and ShuttingDown(). The Typed[T] struct implements these with lock-based synchronization using sync.Cond, maintaining separate dirty and processing sets to handle concurrent access and re-enqueueing of items.\\n\\n**Delaying Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedDelayingInterface extends TypedInterface by adding AddAfter(item, duration) capability, allowing items to be queued for later processing using a priority heap-based delay mechanism. This is essential for implementing backoff and retry logic.\\n\\n**Rate Limiting Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedRateLimitingInterface further extends TypedDelayingInterface by adding rate limiting capabilities through three methods: AddRateLimited(item) which uses the rate limiter to determine when to process an item, Forget(item) to signal completion, and NumRequeues(item) to track retry counts. The rateLimitingType struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and TypedRateLimiter.\\n\\n**Rate Limiters (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):**\\nMultiple rate limiter implementations are provided:\\n- TypedRateLimiter is the base interface with When(item) returning time.Duration, Forget(item), and NumRequeues(item)\\n- TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter implements exponential backoff with baseDelay*2^failures capped at maxDelay\\n- TypedBucketRateLimiter adapts golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter for token bucket rate limiting\\n- TypedMaxOfRateLimiter combines multiple limiters taking the maximum delay\\n- TypedWithMaxWaitRateLimiter caps delays at a maximum threshold\\n- DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter combines ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (per-item) with BucketRateLimiter (overall 10 qps, 100 bucket)\\n\\n**Reconciliation Loop Pattern:**\\nControllers implement the reconciliation pattern across numerous files. The sample controller (staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go) demonstrates the canonical pattern:\\n1. Run() launches worker goroutines calling runWorker()\\n2. runWorker() calls processNextWorkItem() in a loop\\n3. processNextWorkItem() implements the core cycle:\\n   - Call queue.Get() to retrieve next item, returns (item, shutdown)\\n   - Defer queue.Done(item) to mark item as processed\\n   - Call syncHandler(item) to reconcile desired vs actual state\\n   - On success: queue.Forget(item) to stop tracking retry count\\n   - On failure: queue.AddRateLimited(item) to requeue with backoff\\n\\nThis pattern is used across all controllers including: job_controller.go, namespace_controller.go, cronjob_controllerv2.go, endpointslice_controller.go, node_controller.go, route_controller.go, and many more in pkg/controller/ and staging/src/k8s.io/.\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n1. Queue operations are thread-safe and handle concurrent worker access\\n2. The dirty and processing sets prevent duplicate processing while allowing re-enqueueing\\n3. Rate limiting is applied both per-item (exponential backoff) and globally (token bucket)\\n4. The Forget() call is critical - without it, items remain in the rate limiter tracking indefinitely\\n5. across multiple files in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. The system is organized in a layered architecture:\\n\\n**Core Queue Interface (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go):**\\nThe foundation is the TypedInterface which defines the basic work queue operations: Add(item), Get() returning (item, shutdown), Done(item), Len(), ShutDown(), and ShuttingDown(). The Typed[T] struct implements these with lock-based synchronization using sync.Cond, maintaining separate dirty and processing sets to handle concurrent access and re-enqueueing of items.\\n\\n**Delaying Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedDelayingInterface extends TypedInterface by adding AddAfter(item, duration) capability, allowing items to be queued for later processing using a priority heap-based delay mechanism. This is essential for implementing backoff and retry logic.\\n\\n**Rate Limiting Queue (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go):**\\nThe TypedRateLimitingInterface further extends TypedDelayingInterface by adding rate limiting capabilities through three methods: AddRateLimited(item) which uses the rate limiter to determine when to process an item, Forget(item) to signal completion, and NumRequeues(item) to track retry counts. The rateLimitingType struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and TypedRateLimiter.\\n\\n**Rate Limiters (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):**\\nMultiple rate limiter implementations are provided:\\n- TypedRateLimiter is the base interface with When(item) returning time.Duration, Forget(item), and NumRequeues(item)\\n- TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter implements exponential backoff with baseDelay*2^failures capped at maxDelay\\n- TypedBucketRateLimiter adapts golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter for token bucket rate limiting\\n- TypedMaxOfRateLimiter combines multiple limiters taking the maximum delay\\n- TypedWithMaxWaitRateLimiter caps delays at a maximum threshold\\n- DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter combines ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (per-item) with BucketRateLimiter (overall 10 qps, 100 bucket)\\n\\n**Reconciliation Loop Pattern:**\\nControllers implement the reconciliation pattern across numerous files. The sample controller (staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go) demonstrates the canonical pattern:\\n1. Run() launches worker goroutines calling runWorker()\\n2. runWorker() calls processNextWorkItem() in a loop\\n3. processNextWorkItem() implements the core cycle:\\n   - Call queue.Get() to retrieve next item, returns (item, shutdown)\\n   - Defer queue.Done(item) to mark item as processed\\n   - Call syncHandler(item) to reconcile desired vs actual state\\n   - On success: queue.Forget(item) to stop tracking retry count\\n   - On failure: queue.AddRateLimited(item) to requeue with backoff\\n\\nThis pattern is used across all controllers including: job_controller.go, namespace_controller.go, cronjob_controllerv2.go, endpointslice_controller.go, node_controller.go, route_controller.go, and many more in pkg/controller/ and staging/src/k8s.io/.\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n1. Queue operations are thread-safe and handle concurrent worker access\\n2. The dirty and processing sets prevent duplicate processing while allowing re-enqueueing\\n3. Rate limiting is applied both per-item (exponential backoff) and globally (token bucket)\\n4. The Forget() call is critical - without it, items remain in the rate limiter tracking indefinitely\\n5. Multiple workers can safely process different items in parallel while synchronizing through the shared queue\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
